        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1929210403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4076369272654005402"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>You could say that I'm a hardcore Labyrinth fan girl. I love the movie, Labyrinth, and have seen it many times, glitter-dappled set and cheesy puppets aside; it's an interesting story that's clearly inspired by Celtic faerie lore, and (you could argue) the allegorical tale of a girl's coming-of-age through the use of symbolism. In fact, many of the reasons I love the movie are less because of what's <i>in </i>the story and more of what's explic</span>
  <span id="freeText4076369272654005402" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>You could say that I'm a hardcore Labyrinth fan girl. I love the movie, Labyrinth, and have seen it many times, glitter-dappled set and cheesy puppets aside; it's an interesting story that's clearly inspired by Celtic faerie lore, and (you could argue) the allegorical tale of a girl's coming-of-age through the use of symbolism. In fact, many of the reasons I love the movie are less because of what's <i>in </i>the story and more of what's explicitly left <i>out</i>.<br><br><br><br>Because of that, I was a little skeptical when I heard that there was a book coming out that was inspired by Labyrinth - skeptical and also bouncing-off-the-walls excited. Because another book came out this year that was also inspired by one of my favorite stories: RoseBlood by A.G. Howard, <b>which turned one of my favorite antiheroes into a psychic vampire who owns a rave club</b>.<br><br><br><br>I was not pleased with these developments. <br><br><br><br>WINTERSONG starts out okay. It takes place in historical Bavaria, and is about a selfish brat named Elisabeth who only cares about music. She spends most of the book whining, feeling sorry for herself, and being jealous of her siblings. Then one day, her sister, Kathe, is kidnapped by the Goblin King, and Elisabeth is forced to go Underground to save her because if she doesn't succeed, her sister will be gone forever. The integration of <i>The Goblin Market </i>and <i>Der Erlkonig </i>were interesting, but I've seen Labyrinth fanfiction writers run with this concept before. In fact, one of my favorite authors, Subtilior, has a Labyrinth fanfic called <a href="https://www.fanfiction.net/s/3509200/1/Erlk%C3%B6nig" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Erlkönig </b>
</a>that runs with this concept beautifully. Likewise, Viciously Witty has an excellent Labyrinth fic set in Ireland that is based off and called <a href="https://www.fanfiction.net/s/4596100/1/The-Goblin-Market" rel="nofollow noopener"><b>The Goblin Market</b></a>.<br><br>
  <br>
<br>I get that there's only so many famous works of faerie lore, so the possibility of overlap is high, but that just makes it even more important to set your work apart from others' and go the extra mile to make the story interesting and the characters compelling. The Goblin King in WINTERSONG was not compelling. He did not feel like the King of Mischief; he felt like a nervous guy at prom who is afraid that his mean girlfriend is going to embarrass him in front of all his friends. He even blushes and stammers. He's also apparently a christian, or follows christian tenets, since he goes to chapel in his free time and talks a lot about God (especially in the last quarter of the book). This was really jarring to me as a reader, because many of the faerie lore is based on Celtic mythology that predates Christianity by centuries, so it doesn't really make sense that the "Elf King" would go to church....<br><br><br><br>I looked on the author's profile, and in one of her "Ask the Author" questions, when answering how she was inspired to write this story she says she "
  
    decided to write 50 Shades of Labyrinth." So I don't think that it's a stretch to say that WINTERSONG reads like Labyrinth fanfiction, and not even particularly <i>good </i>or original Labyrinth fanfiction, since it primarily relies on ideas that have already been explored by many others in the fandom. Even the sex in this book - arguably the selling point of the premise, since I'm sure many of the hard-core fan girls of Labyrinth wish that there was an alternative telling of the tale when Jareth and Sarah really did end up together - is uninspired and whiny. Elisabeth whines about the sex, that there isn't enough of it, that he doesn't really <i>want </i>her. There are some truly well-written passages in here, but then you also get ridiculous passages like these: "I dip my quill into the inkwell once again, and join up my teardrops into a song" (204).
  
<br><br>
  
    
      <br>
    
  
<br>
  
    If this book is 50 Shades of anything, it's 50 Shades of a Whining Heroine Who Never Shuts the Hell Up. She is one of the most unlikable protagonists I've encountered in a while because all she does is complain and whine and cry and talk about how ugly she is. The only thing that sets the heroine apart are her musical abilities (a similarity it shares with RoseBlood), and she's even a brat about this. She sets her brother's face on fire out of jealousy because he is able to study music because he's a boy and she isn't and gets mad at the Goblin King for obtaining her a klavier because - she says - it's too beautiful for her and that makes her feel bad, basically. I'm sorry, you want me to root for this twit?
  
<br><br>
  
    
      <br>
    
  
<br>
  
    This was a huge disappointment for me. The only upside is that it made me want to go watch Labyrinth again and revisit some of my favorite fanfic to read when I was in college.
  
<br><br>
  
    
      <br>
    
  
<br>1 to 1.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="4076369272654005402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2055006418" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2055006418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3287375499721339438"><b>**3.5-stars**</b><br/><br/><b>Enchanting. Dark. Heartbreaking.</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545423256ra/26785488.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>With the superlatives out of the way, I will admit that the first 50-pages of this were rough. <br/><br/>I wasn't sure what to think but mainly my thoughts were composed of sentiments such as: <br/><br/><i>Do I like this? <br/>Do I actually hate this? <br/>What is going on? <br/><br/><b>How the hell do I pronounce these names???</b></i> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462572690ra/19016162.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>With a little patience, it all started to weave together into an intricate, spellbinding story of forbidden love. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545423256ra/26785490.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Perhaps it makes sense considering the story to view it</span>
  <span id="freeText3287375499721339438" style="display:none"><b>**3.5-stars**</b><br><br><b>Enchanting. Dark. Heartbreaking.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545423256ra/26785488.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>With the superlatives out of the way, I will admit that the first 50-pages of this were rough. <br><br>I wasn't sure what to think but mainly my thoughts were composed of sentiments such as: <br><br><i>Do I like this? <br>Do I actually hate this? <br>What is going on? <br><br><b>How the hell do I pronounce these names???</b></i> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462572690ra/19016162.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>With a little patience, it all started to weave together into an intricate, spellbinding story of forbidden love. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545423256ra/26785490.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Perhaps it makes sense considering the story to view it as a musical composition: timid at first as the story begins to unfold, solid and constant through the middle then a resounding crescendo as we rush towards our ultimate conclusion.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545423256ra/26785489.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>I was surprised that the romance element of this work for me. I usually am not into whimsical romances, but for some reason this one worked for me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545423256ra/26785491.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are definitely some steamy elements. I even blushed once or twice!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469712758ra/19849374.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The love between Elisabeth and her Goblin King is somehow fractious, violent and childish all at the same time. <br><br>Their connection is so tangible, I felt it in my heart; the ups and downs of their lustful and rough coming together. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487803319ra/22052850.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The musical elements of the story were beautiful. They helped to bring it alive for me. If this were to be turned into a movie, I believe it would have an absolutely revolutionary soundtrack! <br><br>Overall, I felt drawn into the story, slowly but surely and once I was in, I was in, <b>entire</b>. I cannot wait to read the next book of the series!</span>

<div id="review_1993675891" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1993675891" />
    <a title="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews"><img alt="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492999740p2/66199133.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1993675891?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" href="/user/show/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews">Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=reviews-of-the-year">reviews-of-the-year</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=fey">fey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=favorite-heroine">favorite-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=guilty-pleasure">guilty-pleasure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=hot-jerks">hot-jerks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=magic-etc">magic-etc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1993675891" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17929880375575651180">This book had the greatest beginning of all time: I am <b>CHALLENGING</b> everyone who reads this review to find a better one than this!!<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Winter turned to spring, spring to summer, summer into autumn, autumn back into winter, but each turning of the year grew harder and harder as the little girl grew up while the Goblin King remained the same. She washed the dishes, cleaned the floors, brushed her sister’s hair, soothed her brother’s fears, hid her father’s purse, counted the coins, and no long</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText17929880375575651180" style="display:none">This book had the greatest beginning of all time: I am <b>CHALLENGING</b> everyone who reads this review to find a better one than this!!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Winter turned to spring, spring to summer, summer into autumn, autumn back into winter, but each turning of the year grew harder and harder as the little girl grew up while the Goblin King remained the same. She washed the dishes, cleaned the floors, brushed her sister’s hair, soothed her brother’s fears, hid her father’s purse, counted the coins, and no longer went into the woods to see her old friend.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>A FREAKING PERFECT BEGINNING of introducing a world where magic is hidden/not the norm but exists, a girl who use to be part of that world but eventually left for "reality" but the Goblin king <u>never</u> forgets a bargain..muahha<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499186480ra/23202562.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499186480ra/23202558.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Käthe made a face. “It’s always about Josef with you. Don’t you have any dreams of your own?”<br>I did. They were locked up in a box, safe and sound beneath the bed we shared, never to be seen, never to be heard.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The burden of being <b>Lisel</b>, the responsible older sister and dutiful eldest daughter who must always put her needs above others. At times it was scary how much I related to this character and the sibling relationships were done sooo well. You know characters are well developed when you want to physically <b>punch</b> their face. So good job! <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Tsk, tsk.” The Goblin King waved one long, slender finger at me. “I had thought you a worthy opponent. We were playing a game, Fräulein, but you don’t seem much inclined to engage me.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Its the best game in the world: one where he takes what you love and hides it. And if you don't come find it then its his forever. <b>A game that forces you to make selfish and selfless decisions.</b> I'll be perfectly honest guys I am wayyyy to emotionally invested in this plot. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499186480ra/23202559.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>AND THAT PLOT TWIST !<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Liesl,” Josef said again. “I’m so very glad you’re safe. But I must ask you: who have you been searching for? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[None of us understand what you’ve been talking about. Who, my dear, is Käthe?” <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Oh SNAP WHAT THE FUCK FUCK OH THAT GOLBIN FUCKING TRICKERY KING <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499186480ra/23202561.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> In this treacherous game, <b>the Goblin king has his tricks but Liesls has her stubborness....</b>we shall see who prevails in the end *Stubborness all the way i believe in you Liesl!!*<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“And what had I done with the Goblin King’s gift? I had taken it and hidden it away, like it was something secret, something shameful. Perhaps my lack of faith had cost me everything after all.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This is where true writing shows: the classic -show don't just tell- was so prominent and well done in this book I wanted to cry. The author <b>DID NOT</b> just simply tell us over and over again about the wisdom of Liesl and how smart she is and what a good sister, BLAH, BLAH, BLAH!!! The author <b>
  <u>showed</u>
</b> her love of her family through her sacrifices and her thought<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499186480ra/23202560.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“So I tried my best to stifle hope. Because hope’s twin was despair, and despair was infinitely worse. If hope hurt, then despair was the absence of hurt. It was the absence of feeling. It was the absence of caring.<br>I wanted very much to care.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>This is one of the most beautiful and powerful descriptions i have ever read that really showed the struggle of a character to just enrapture us reader. The only thing worse than caring, is not caring at all and I feel like a lot of people would relate to struggles Liesl went through. <b>Being in the goblin world, she slowly looses her spark/energy and I know we can all think of places that drain our own spark. </b> <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I am Elisabeth,” I said. “But Elisabeth is only a name. An empty word I fill with myself. But you had a word once; I see the echoes of it within you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>This part of the book had me on the edge of my seats. This silly girl with music in her heasrts turned out to be so much more. <b>Short-tempered yet disciplined. Self-indulgent, selfish, yet selfless. She is compassion, hatred, and contradiction all in one.</b> I love Liesl as a character with a deeper understanding than most. I related to her like no other and she helped me with my own shit and this description really soothed me.<br><br><b> And the Golbin king? I would actually kill to find out his name.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499186480ra/23202557.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now for my complaints:<br>1. While the goblin kingdom was meant to be mysterious at times it seemed incomplete <br>2. While i did love the emphasis on character development, the actual actions were less than satisfied with the most chaotic thing being a simple ball at the beginning<br>3. Brief skim over the siren creatures that are part of their world but not...?<br>4. I have others but right now i'm on a book high and i just loved this novel<br><br><b> The wait and agony for book two is slowly killing me, <u>so obviously you all need to read this to share my pain ;)</u></b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17929880375575651180" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court"><img alt="High Lady of The Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556501727p2/62560505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2330616705?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court?shelf=fantasy-read">fantasy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2330616705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10636605434672280309"><i>
  <b> A dark,musical, and twisted love story filled with confusion, hatred, and dread. </b>
</i><br/><br/>The second I read the first page I knew there was no backing out of this story. I knew I would start and finish it with no interruption.<br/><br/>The moment you start this book, I still can't comprehend how, the story pulls you in like wines wrapping themselves around you and pulling you in. The entire book has this air of mystery surrounding it even if we know what's happening so it constantly keeps you wanting to read </span>
  <span id="freeText10636605434672280309" style="display:none"><i>
  <b> A dark,musical, and twisted love story filled with confusion, hatred, and dread. </b>
</i><br /><br />The second I read the first page I knew there was no backing out of this story. I knew I would start and finish it with no interruption.<br /><br />The moment you start this book, I still can't comprehend how, the story pulls you in like wines wrapping themselves around you and pulling you in. The entire book has this air of mystery surrounding it even if we know what's happening so it constantly keeps you wanting to read more. After I got past the first 3 chapters, I hardly noticed how much time has passed and all of a sudden I was done with the book.<br /><br />We follow Elisabeth as she discovers that the stories her delusional grandmother fixates about are quite real and that she should have heeded her warning. Elisabeth finds out that the Goblin King is real, and now he has taken her sister to the Underworld in order to make her his next queen. Instead, Elisabeth bargains for her sisters freedom and in exchange, agrees to marry him. As she navigates this world of eternal winter, she appeals to another side of the Goblin King and realizes that he is not just the wild, Lord of Mischief he pretends to be.<br /><br />Elisabeth is definitely not one of my favorite protagonists. Whenever she talks about her sister in the beginning of the book, it feels like a part of her is constantly insulting her sister but a part of her remains jealous of her. She is envious of her brother's talents and makes a point of saying she is nothing compared to him, which gets annoying after some time. Her relationship with the goblin king is most definitely not what you would call an ideal romance and a lot of her time in the underworld is miserable. <br /><br />After that you would think I didn't like the book, but I did enjoy it. It was interesting to see how the story would continue and what would happen to the characters. The world was definitely very unique as I don't usually see many perspectives on the 'goblin king' and a lot of my questions do remain unanswered but I look forward to seeing what is revealed in the next and final installment of this duology. This book gets a 4 from me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10636605434672280309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2013082837" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2013082837" />
    <a title="Always Pouting" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting"><img alt="Always Pouting" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483476563p2/48650982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2013082837?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Always Pouting" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Always Pouting" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting">Always Pouting</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2013082837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer300429724841107156">Liesl has always been a responsible older sister, looking after her younger sister Kathe and sacrificing her own dreams for her brother Josef. Lisel will never be beautiful like Kathe is and her music will forever live in the shadow of Josef's virtuoso abilities. Though she longs to give into her own desires, she forces herself to be self sacrificing. Then strange things begin to happen and Kathe disappears and no one but Liesl remembers she even exists. Though her grandma always told them stori</span>
  <span id="freeText300429724841107156" style="display:none">Liesl has always been a responsible older sister, looking after her younger sister Kathe and sacrificing her own dreams for her brother Josef. Lisel will never be beautiful like Kathe is and her music will forever live in the shadow of Josef's virtuoso abilities. Though she longs to give into her own desires, she forces herself to be self sacrificing. Then strange things begin to happen and Kathe disappears and no one but Liesl remembers she even exists. Though her grandma always told them stories about goblins, Liesl never believed in them, even with the uncanny childhood memories of playing the wood with a small boy that she can't explain. Kathe's disappearance brings the truth to light as Liesl must journey to the underworld and save her sister, eventually sacrificing herself to the Goblin King in her sister's place. <br /><br />Like a lot of people I really enjoyed the beginning of the book but I think that by the second half the pacing got a little slow. The writing was really good but that doesn't help when it starts to feel like the plot is dragging. Especially when Liesl keep ruminating over how plain she is, which really wouldn't have bothered me if the story moved faster. I think some parts could have been done without in the book like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Josef being a changeling or Liesl taking so long to figure out how to leave as well as to find Kathe or the whole thing with Kathe's engagement <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I understand that the author was trying to build up the relationship between Liesl and the Goblin King but the both were brooding too much and I would rather kept moving forward with things. Also I found the ending sort of unsatisfying though I'm not sure what I would have preferred happen. All in all it was really well written and I enjoyed it but I wish the pacing was better and there was less repetition about certain things like Liesl's insecurities. I really loved the underlying burning desire that Liesl was trying to suppress and the way it's brought out in her, that was really well done I could almost feel it myself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="300429724841107156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1923972788" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1923972788" />
    <a title="Tanya Tate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46136280-tanya-tate"><img alt="Tanya Tate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605108821p2/46136280.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1923972788?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanya Tate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanya Tate" href="/user/show/46136280-tanya-tate">Tanya Tate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29763799-wintersong">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46136280-tanya-tate?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46136280-tanya-tate?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46136280-tanya-tate?shelf=nope">nope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46136280-tanya-tate?shelf=whinny-protag">whinny-protag</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46136280-tanya-tate?shelf=i-wish-i-could-have-loved-you">i-wish-i-could-have-loved-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46136280-tanya-tate?shelf=a-waste-of-time">a-waste-of-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1923972788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1112290432936984705">Edit 2: As of March 19,2018 ,this review has 100 likes on it! That's the most likes have on any of my reviews. Who knew a book i didn't like would get so many likes? lol I'm also putting the link of my review from my blog on here as well. <br/><br/>Edit: I got a fourth point that makes it problematic for me. <br/><br/>Spoilers and Rant mode time<br/> <br/><a href='https://tanyasreading.wordpress.com/2017/02/28/wintersong-by-s-jae-jones/' rel='nofollow noopener'> You can also read it on my blog! </a><br/><br/>DNF@72% 1 Star<br/><br/>I tried so hard to finish this but I couldn't.<br/><br/>I thought after I got halfway through it would get better which it did but the</span>
  <span id="freeText1112290432936984705" style="display:none">Edit 2: As of March 19,2018 ,this review has 100 likes on it! That's the most likes have on any of my reviews. Who knew a book i didn't like would get so many likes? lol I'm also putting the link of my review from my blog on here as well. <br /><br />Edit: I got a fourth point that makes it problematic for me. <br /><br />Spoilers and Rant mode time<br /> <br /><a href="https://tanyasreading.wordpress.com/2017/02/28/wintersong-by-s-jae-jones/" rel="nofollow noopener"> You can also read it on my blog! </a><br /><br />DNF@72% 1 Star<br /><br />I tried so hard to finish this but I couldn't.<br /><br />I thought after I got halfway through it would get better which it did but then it just fell through for me. <br /><br />I went through the MC whining about her being plain and not desired by anyone, her being jealous of her sister being a "woman" but sort of slut shaming her and her being jealous brother musical talent which was borderline obsession cause she was kind of using him for her own musical ambitions since she was the composer, her not being on good terms with her dad and being label as the forgotten sister to her talented brother and her being hot and cold with the goblin king. ( which was the only saving grace of this book) <br /><br />Four things that broke it for me which the author did cause I feel like it was problematic. <br /><br />1. The author created all this sexual tension between Goblin King and the MC ( I'm not going to try and spell it. ) with them having heavy make outs ,touching, and them both saying they want each other and couldn't even follow through properly. Meaning that you didn't follow through with sex being implied or fade into black if you didn't want to go into full detail. ( But hell She was 19 and you teetering on the edge of New Adult in the first place with the sexual tension so in all honesty...but I digress. The whole YA/NA is a discussion for another time.) Your readers shouldn't have to play the guessing game when it comes to something as important as that. <br /><br />2. The author choosing to have her MC bleed as a way to saying that she's not a virgin anymore and it being the only proof that they did have sex. How many freaking books and fanfics are going to use this tried stereotypical trope?? That it has been proven by science that if the vagina is properly lubricated that the female will not bleed? That bleeding is not a indication of a woman being a virgin? So why it's still being used? ?? WHY?? All she could have said was her being sore and that's it. <br /><br />3. The fact the MC finally feels like she stepped into womanhood by giving herself to the goblin king and now finally being able to give herself to the music fully even though the Goblin King has tried so hard for her to open up to her musical side without going to that route yet. That he went through all those unethical things in order for her to become his bride( like kidnapping her sister) so he can awaken her musical side which he know she had hidden inside her since she was a kid. . Are you kidding me? Are you mean to tell me that now since she's not a virgin anymore that she can finally compose music like she should? What the hell?? It's just plays on the stereotype that sex is a rite into womanhood which shouldn't be the case at all. I mean what are you telling your young teenage female readers who are reading this?? What message are you sending?? Especially to your readers who maybe coming to turns with themselves as being asexual...... <br /><br />4. The fact the MC kept insisting the Goblin King to have sex with her and he constantly told her no. It got so cringe worthy to me that I honestly thought that she was going to rape him. She also threw a temper tantrum because of it. Now if this was flipped the other way that the MC was telling him no and he kept insisting they have sex I wonder how many five stars it will would have??*sips tea* <br /><br />If those four things didn't happen, this book was looking at least a 2.5 or 3 stars for me cause it did keep my interest to that point even tho I wanted to hit the MC so many times. Also the fact this is the second book I read this month that I couldn't stand with older sister/young sister dynamic.With the older sister have to save the younger sister from herself. (cough caraval) Being a little sister myself, I can't stand how younger sisters are always being portrayed as being wild and free.. While the older sister is being portrayed as being jealous of the younger sister. Not all little sisters or Old/Younger sisters dynamic is like that and it's a trope that needs to be squashed. I can tell you that my sister is the most supportive people I have and she more carefree than I am. Hell she have tell me multiple times that I need to stop being so hard of myself cause I'm far from being carefree and wild. <br /><br />It's a few other things that got me which was the " You not like other girls" line from a side character which is very stereotypical and the repetitive writing. I keep saying that you shouldn't play down to your audience. That you don't have to constantly remind them of certain things. <br /><br />The only saving grace of this book was the Goblin King even if some of his methods was problematic at best.. He still an interesting character up to that point. <br /><br />But after that I can't finish it and I wasted two days listening to this.<br /><br />So another one bites the dust. <br /><br />One more thing. I saw that Renee Ahdieh rated it five stars I'm like " You wrote a better romance and fade into black scene than that with Wrath and the Dawn!" smh<br /><br />NEXT!</span>

<div id="review_1460223993" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Roshani Chokshi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26262898-roshani-chokshi"><img alt="Roshani Chokshi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544538349p2/26262898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1460223993?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roshani Chokshi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roshani Chokshi" href="/user/show/26262898-roshani-chokshi">Roshani Chokshi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1460223993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12839964856950719433">This was Labyrinth by way of Angela Carter, and I think my soul has been aching for a book like WINTERSONG for the last decade. Deliciously romantic with a nuanced Goblin King figure (fancast: Tom Hiddleston) and a strong heroine, this story was rife with fairytales and music and enchantment. It's also more than a little sexy. No complaints here.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1871315763" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1871315763" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42163117-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508217767p2/42163117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1871315763?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/42163117-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1871315763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18116046153658528679">2 stars. <br/><br/>(<b>edit:</b> this book popped back up on my feed today, and considering how <i>livid</i> even thinking about it makes me, I'm bumping my rating down another half star. I really am still being generous here.)<br/><br/>Mmmmmmmmmm I have a lot of thoughts and feelings about this book.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499398401ra/23227193.gif' width='480' height='270' alt='sipstea' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I was <i>so sure</i> I was going to love this. The blurb made it sound so mysterious and creepy and intriguing: a young musician gets caught up with evil goblins who steal her sister, and she has to find a way into a dark underworld to sav</span>
  <span id="freeText18116046153658528679" style="display:none">2 stars. <br><br>(<b>edit:</b> this book popped back up on my feed today, and considering how <i>livid</i> even thinking about it makes me, I'm bumping my rating down another half star. I really am still being generous here.)<br><br>Mmmmmmmmmm I have a lot of thoughts and feelings about this book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499398401ra/23227193.gif" width="480" height="270" alt="sipstea" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was <i>so sure</i> I was going to love this. The blurb made it sound so mysterious and creepy and intriguing: a young musician gets caught up with evil goblins who steal her sister, and she has to find a way into a dark underworld to save her. Music. Creepy faeries. Underground lairs. Strong sibling relationships. Twisty, mysterious plots. <b>THIS HAD SO MUCH POTENTIAL.</b> Also, I know this has nothing to do with the book’s content, but the cover is GORGEOUS, <i>and</i> I was buddy reading this with a lovely human <s>(which still ended up being a lot of fun even if we lowkey hated this)</s>.<br><br>So you could say I was excited.<br><br>And the first quarter of this was pretty fucking great. It was exactly what I wanted: a mysterious and eerie mix of fairytale and psychological thriller, with a hint of paranormal romance. The writing was <i>beautiful.</i> I seriously felt like I should have been reading this book on a winter evening while sipping mulled wine and eating pomegranate seeds. <s>As bitter as I am about the rest of this book, I feel obligated to give this two stars for the writing.</s><br><br>(Also: where does one acquire a creepy superstitious grandma who makes ominous predictions about faeries because <i>I want one.</i>)<br><br>All of the atmospheric writing and hauntingly beautiful details of the world really pulled me in, enough so that I was able to overlook the characters’ flaws.<br><br>Or at least, that was how it worked until about the midway point. Somewhere around the beginning of Part 3, everything I was enjoying about this completely fell to pieces. Liesl’s relationships with her family members, all of the mysterious trickery and manipulations that the plot of the first half had going on…..<i>all of that disappeared.</i> It became abruptly clear that this was not, in fact, a story about a musician outsmarting creepy goblins and making sacrifices for family members……it was a cringey, bizarre romance with random tangents about music and an overabundance of sex scenes that made me want to bleach my eyes. <br><br>(This section is going to be a mini-rant, because there was almost nothing I enjoyed about the second half of the book.)<br><br>First of all, the worldbuilding was completely thrown out. (We learn the barest essentials by the end, but so much is left unexplained and poorly developed.) None of the promises of a rich, fascinating underworld that I got from the first third of the book were fulfilled. There were so many weird inconsistencies. Uggghhhh I don’t even want to go into it, I felt so let down.<br><br>Pretty much all of the characters from the first half of the book completely disappeared. Liesl’s mother, father, grandmother, siblings, the other minor characters…it felt like their existence was ultimately unnecessary, as the bulk of the main story consisted of Liesl and the Goblin King’s creepy, angst-ridden relationship.<br><br>And let’s talk about that relationship, shall we?<br><br>I’ve mentioned this in a few reviews before, but I’d like to start out by saying that instalove is not <i>inherently</i> terrible. It can work in some books, and it has worked for me in a number of books I’ve loved. Unfortunately, this was not one of them.<br><br>Allow me to introduce our “love interest.” <br><br>Liesl met the Goblin King when she was a small child. They played and sang songs together in the woods when she was young, but as a teen she believes those memories to be nothing more than figments of her imagination. However, the Goblin King has never forgotten her, nor the promise Liesl apparently made that she would marry him when she grew up.<br><br>Before I move any further, I just want to stop and say how weird and creepy (not good creepy, <b>bad</b> creepy) I thought this whole premise was. The Goblin King repeatedly complains about how Liesl is different now, how he liked Liesl better when she was little, how she’s changed too much, and it was almost vaguely pedophilic to me. He continued to romanticize how Liesl had been as a young child, despite her repeated attempts to remind him that she is different because she has grown up and matured. I wasn’t buying into this supposed connection they had <i>at all</i>.<br><br>But that isn’t even the tip of the fucking iceberg. (And when I say iceberg, I don’t mean huge, spiky, and terrifying chunk of frozen water that sinks ships, I mean the bland, tasteless, and sad type of lettuce that you get on really boring salads.) This book tried <i>so hard</i> to be Edgy™, but it was just dull, frustratingly anti-feminist, and ultimately quite predictable and cheesy.<br><br>I really don't care for the romantic trope in which an otherwise plain and unremarkable girl only learns to define her identity and embrace herself by extension of her relationship with a man. This theme was pretty much shoved down the reader’s throat throughout the book in no uncertain terms: the majority of the plot in the second half consists of Liesl trying to pressure the Goblin King to have sex with her, pushing herself on him and groping him as he repeatedly tells her "no". (The fact that she actually assaults him is never brought up or challenged, either, because apparently it's ~empowering~ when a woman forces herself on a man.) 🙄🙄<br><br>After he finally gives in, Liesl spends pages waxing poetic about how he “made her into a woman” and “everything was changed now”. She very literally defines her life into “Before” and “After” this happens, blabbering on nonstop about how her sexual relationship has allowed her to finally discover her own sense of self. Now, I’m all for everyone being able to feel free to have their own sex life on their own terms, but their relationship just seemed <i>incredibly</i> unhealthy (not to mention mostly of the language used is blatantly aphobic). Liesl spent all this time trying to pressure the Goblin King to sleep with her because she needed validation that she was “desirable.” She’s entirely reliant on his affection to maintain her own image of self-worth. And as I mentioned, the worst part is that this behavior is portrayed as some sort of empowerment.<br><br>Also….can we talk about how many fucking music metaphors were used in their sex scenes?????? I’m sorry but it was <i>cringey af</i> and I was Not Into It™.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I was wound tighter than a violin string, pitched too sharp, and I urged his rough, callused fingertips lower, loosening me, tuning me to the right key.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444222453ra/16471852.gif" width="480" height="255" alt="octopusno" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There’s also this weird double standard when it comes to how sex is viewed??????? Like, Liesl is allowed to have a liberating sexual awakening, but her sister Käthe—who is consistently characterized as a pretty, flirty, superficial Mary Sue—is essentially seen as a shallow slut by both Liesl and the Goblin King. Liesl had a very “I’m not like other girls” attitude and it pissed me off.<br><br>The only part of the book I consistently liked was Josef. He was so sweet and pure and too good for the rest of the characters, he didn’t deserve to be in the middle of this mess. And <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ that plot twist!!!!!! I really loved that reveal, and I lowkey only wanna read the next book to see what happens with him. also can we talk about how he is literally surviving on François’s love??????? MY FUCKING HEART MAN. Why is this book not their love story instead of L*esl and the G*blin K*ng, I don’t get it  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I feel conflicted about including a fav quotes section bc I’m still so pissed at this book for catfishing me with that pretty cover and description. The writing really was beautiful, though, and I have all these quotes I highlighted (mostly from back when I was actually enjoying the book) sooooo here they are:<br><br><i>"You smolder, mistress. There is a fire burning within you, but it is a slow burn. It shimmers with heat, waiting only for a breath to fan it to life.”<br><br>His voice was neither deep nor high, but there was a quality to it that spoke of dark woods and dry winter nights.<br><br>"There is music in your soul. A wild and untamed sort of music that speaks to me. It defies all the rules and laws you humans set upon it. It grows inside you, and I have a wish to set that music free.”<br><br>Her words shook something loose in my mind, my thoughts scattering to the floor like falling leaves. But they were only scant impressions—feathers, ice, pale eyes—that disappeared as soon as I tried to hold them, like snowflakes in my hand.<br>“The music.”<br>“What music?” That half-woken memory tickled again, an itch I could not scratch.<br>“Tut,” she said, turning her smile on me. ”You, of all people, should have recognized it. Can you not hear the sound of your own soul singing?”<br><br>I am a wild thing, a creature of the forest and the storm and the night. I run through dreams and fancies, through all the stories of my childhood of the dark and uncanny and strange and weird. <br><br>This was the immortality humans were meant to have: to be remembered by those who loved us long after our bodies had crumbled into dust.</i><br><br>-------------------------------------<br><br>BR with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42130592-kazzexual" rel="nofollow noopener">the obscure hp quote expert</a> &lt;3</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="18116046153658528679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText3196443826008890185" style="display:none">Dude. Duuuuuuuude. This. Book. Messed me uuuup. <br><br>It was slow to start for me. I thought I wasn’t going to like it very much but then sweet Elisabeth went underground AND HUNG OUT WITH THE GOBLIN KING. I was hooked from the moment she went underground. So hooked that I just read over half of this book in one day. I just couldn’t put it down!!<br><br>I loved Elisabeth as a main character. Her whole life she has been told she’s not good enough, not pretty enough, just not enough. She found herself in the underground and started believing she was beautiful on the inside, and that’s what makes her a beautiful person. <br><br>The Goblin King. CAN WE JUST TAKE A MOMENT???? He was such a well written love interest. The way he treated Elisabeth was too much for me to handle sometimes because GOALS. <br><br>Josef🖤🖤🖤 Josef was a blessing. I, too have a little brother that is half of my soul and boi did I relate to their relationship!! I really liked him and his love interest as well. <br><br>BOOK TWO BETTER HAVE MORE TWIG IN IT. THAT SWEET SOUL, OH MY LORDT. I adore her. <br><br>One thing I do want to mention, there’s loads about music in here. I ate. it. up. I was in band and choir growing up, so I understood the technical lingo that was used, but other people may not. It’s really a big chunk of the book, so if you’re not into music, or don’t really know how writing/reading music works, you may not like this book very much. <br><br>ALSO. There are some steamy bits FOR SURE. They aren’t as graphic as ACOMAF or anything, but they are very present. <br><br>CAN’T WAIT FOR SHADOWSONG💜❤️💜❤️<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1531252044i/25952665._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1531252045i/25952666._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1531252045i/25952667._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="3196443826008890185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1943951049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1849582474539441043"><br/>This is a story about a brave maiden. This is a story of a tragedy. This is a story about the power of love. This is a story about the compassion and love and sacrifice between siblings. This is a story about selfishness and selflessness. This is the story of the greatest sacrifice. This is a story about life.<br/><br/><i> “Beware the goblin men and the wares they sell.”</i><br/><br/>This book is magical. The writing is exquisite. The world is so encompassing and real. The characters are flawed and selfish and selfless an</span>
  <span id="freeText1849582474539441043" style="display:none"><br />This is a story about a brave maiden. This is a story of a tragedy. This is a story about the power of love. This is a story about the compassion and love and sacrifice between siblings. This is a story about selfishness and selflessness. This is the story of the greatest sacrifice. This is a story about life.<br /><br /><i> “Beware the goblin men and the wares they sell.”</i><br /><br />This book is magical. The writing is exquisite. The world is so encompassing and real. The characters are flawed and selfish and selfless and strong, so so strong.<br /><br />There’s so much passion and love and fire and emotion. The book winds you up in its magic and takes you on this rollercoaster that you can’t get off even if you wanted to ((which let’s be real, you don’t want to))<br /><br />I am absolutely enchanted. I am absolutely shattered and heartbroken and mourning. <br /><br />Someone help me this book has exceeded my highest expectations and ended on a note that I cannot bear. <br /><br />W O W<br /><br />Okay, I have no more words beyond that I’m going to go sob for a while and get dehydrated over it. That’s how good it is. I’m legit out of words.<br /><br /><i> “She was the sun and he was the earth waking from a thaw.”</i><br /><br />5 stars!!<br /><br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Buddy read </i>
</b> with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10502567" rel="nofollow noopener">Jianamin</a></span>

<div id="review_1633110393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1633110393" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1633110393?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1633110393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12228968474915012903"><b>"What's the use of running, if we are on the wrong road?"</b><br/><br/>First notes. They are enchanting. Haunting. Alluring- no, no, what are you saying? It's something else. They <i>are</i> the enchantment. They are the ghost and the obsession. They are the allure.<br/>The difference is slight, almost indiscernible -one could say it exist only if you <i>will</i> it into existence- but it's there. And since it's there, since these notes don't make you feel, but <i>are</i> the feel, the space between them is filled with promise. The st</span>
  <span id="freeText12228968474915012903" style="display:none"><b>"What's the use of running, if we are on the wrong road?"</b><br /><br />First notes. They are enchanting. Haunting. Alluring- no, no, what are you saying? It's something else. They <i>are</i> the enchantment. They are the ghost and the obsession. They are the allure.<br />The difference is slight, almost indiscernible -one could say it exist only if you <i>will</i> it into existence- but it's there. And since it's there, since these notes don't make you feel, but <i>are</i> the feel, the space between them is filled with promise. The staff is bursting with it, full to the brim, the spaces insufficient, the lines painfully bulging. <br />Paradoxically, they should explode. For the song to fulfill its crescendo, <b>they should explode</b>. Dissolve in the river gushing from within them.<br /><b>They never do</b>.<br /><br />The boy you've been crushing on for so many months you forgot how it is not to adore him, on a lucky and maybe a little tipsy night finally kisses you. He gently backs you in a corner and even more gently kisses you. You are stunned blissful, overjoyed, and you wait for the shock to wear off so you can properly enjoy the moment. You wait and wait and wait, and the shock does wear off. And you wait and wait and wait. Something is still missing, but <b>you are faithful</b>. You can't have waited all that time for such a plain thing. And so you wait and wait and wait. <i>It must come. It's just here around the corner. It must be so</i>. <br />But it isn't, and<b> the magic never comes</b>.<br /><br />The next metaphor is far less pretty, but we are not striving for prettiness.<br /><br /><i>[aside] <br />Or are we?</i><br /><br />Do you know when your nose prickles, and your eyes start to water a little, and the muscle in you upper lip twitch just the littlest bit? Of course you know. And you know what it means. it means, trivially put, that you need to sneeze. I am also sure you know how unpleasant and irksome it is when the sneeze doesn't actually come.<br />I feel as if <b>I just had to sneeze</b>, <b>and couldn't</b>.<br /><br />•<i>Wintersong</i> (rightfully) has the pretension of bringing you into a magical world without trotting out impossible tasks or adventurous journeys. Since I am not much of a lover of plot-driven books, this is, to me, <b>a real asset</b>. The book hasn't got any plot twist worth the name, and I always appreciate not only this fact in itself, but the audacity it takes for an author to bet on a plot of this kind and stake their hopes on it. The novel, however, presents unmistakable <b>pace issues</b> that, sadly, blemish its faultless façade. For one thing, the first part, concerning <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Käthe's abduction <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, drags out much too long, considering that it isn't even the point. The middle part is absolutely dull (I wonder if that counts as an oxymoron?) and grey and uninteresting. The chapter leading up to the grand finale grandly fail to build up the climax. Things happen without a reason or a later reference or meaning, as if they were meant simply to fill up some dozens of pages. Instead of neatly rearranging itself in a ball, <b>the thread of this story unfolds and unfolds meaninglessly, aimlessly, heading nowhere</b> in such a blatant state of confusion I could not, for the life of me, turn a blind eye on it. The rhythm was off; the song did not catch my ear.<br /><br />•<b>More folklore would have definitely spiced things up</b>. Have you ever seen <i>After Earth</i>, the movie? When I'm asked what I think about it, my usual answer is that even though it is set on a post-apocalyptic Earth, it might as well have been set on another planet, and that did not make sense to me. Here is the same: readers, meet the <b>goblin people</b>. They're nasty, they're mischievous, they're absolutely similar to any other sprite you can think of. Some of them are kind of kind. And there are changelings too: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>they are born from wishes</b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Think that is cool? Want to go deeper into that? Forget it. Because apparently, <b>the romance was more important than some proper world-building</b>.<br /><br />•Yes, <b>the romance</b>. I unfortunately did not feel it. I understood the development of their relationship on a rational level, but it did not, not even in the slightest, touch me. I tend to blame it on the <b>partial lack of characterization</b> -and I know I have to provide further information on that "partial". <br />The book generally exceeds in tell and lacks in show. Throughout all the first part of the novel, we're told, repeatedly, how Liesl feels miserable, unwanted, neglected, but we're not told <i>why</i>, or rather, we are not shown. Later in the book we are, through (<i>hardly</i>, honestly; but at least we had those) a couple of instances, but it felt like too late. First, you've got to wonder what's gotten into her for about two-hundred pages. Not pretty. Moreover, she comes off as a <b>monotonous</b> and unvarying, in spite of the fact that her change, her growth, is supposed to be the main point of the book. Again, not pretty. I hoped she would become more tolerable as soon as she grew tired of <b>play victim</b>, but although the change really was noticeable in some ways, it did nothing to allow me to connect with her. <br /><br />•Not even <b>the Goblin King</b> fully convinced me, but there's a thing about his character that I absolutely loved and that, in my opinion, wasn't fully developed and exploited by the author: <b>the Goblin King, at first, undeniably acts out of selfishness and spite</b>. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He decides to do Elisabeth wrong basically because he's cross with her. He could let her go in the first place, let her forget him and live, if without excitement, without fear as well, but he doesn't. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And not because he wants her to bloom; only because he wants to indulge his caprice. Such<b> malice</b> is so unusual in ya books, I couldn't help but adoring it, and I am a little bewildered S. Jae-Jones didn't play on it more, because it really looks like a winning point to me. Besides, it makes the character development stand out even more, because<b> at last <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he regrets his actions and really lets her go <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></b>. To me, <i>this</i> was the point of the Goblin King's character and the most beautiful and <b>poignant</b> thing about him, but it kind of got lost among many other less striking things, who knows how.<br />On the other hand, since, as I already said, the timing and the writing of the book don't really do their job,<b> his background (and its revelation too) left me completely indifferent</b>. And, sorry if I repeat myself,<b> the problem lied not in the contents, but in the form</b>.<br /><br />•<b>The ending</b> is the strangest and most curious and most surprising thing the novel, in general, has to offer. It is neither happy nor sad, but a perfect <b>middle ground</b>. It is the ending that finally, actually shows Liesl's full potential as a <b>heroine</b>, because that's what Liesl is in this ending, a heroine. She is confused (in the sense that her character seems to be clueless as to where its narrative purpose lies) and ineffective throughout the whole book, but <b>now and here is where she finds herself</b>. Loved loved loved it. <br /><br />•But since this is no candy land, of course the ending too must cross me somehow. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The world will die and wither if the Underwold doesn't receive a sacrifice. So Liesl sacrifices herself; we even see how the world actually threatens to plunge into eternal winter when she so much as steps outside of her husband's dominion. And then she can just un-sacrifice herself like that, and the world continues existing happily ever after? Does this mean, what? That a sacrifice is no longer requested? If that's the case, why, and how is that possible when the whole plot basically stems from that? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br />The word that automatically pops to my mind is <b>convenient</b>. I really can't stand when authors do that, bending the rules they set themselves so the story can flow on undisturbed. If you don't want to or can't stick to those rules, change them, switch them with new ones, and if you need exceptions, <b>arrange for the exceptions to be rules in the first place</b>. What's the fun part of <b>creating</b>, if not this?<br /><br />•All the other characters were too poorly shaped for me to really form an opinion about any of them -which speaks volumes. Basically, <i>Wintersong</i> features only three characters, the third being made one half from Käthe and the other from Josef.<br /><br />•I'll puke my guts out if I hear again the phrase "music in [whoever's] soul".<br /><br />➽ If I could talk music, I would probably find the right terms to wittily sum this up talking about clefs and moods throwing around random Italian words (and believe me, <i>that</i> I can do), but I don't talk music, not at those levels. So I'll put it simply: <b>although the potential was all there, the execution wasn't satisfying to me</b>. It felt hollow and unsure; very<b> heartfelt</b> indeed, and passionate, but paradoxically I could only take it in with my mind, my heart untouched, and, as if that were not enough, my mind as well found a thing or two to say. What I am profoundly grateful for is <b>that ending</b>: that <b>alone is</b> surely <b>worth the whole book</b>, which, I hope, will prove to be nothing like any other ya you've read before. If that's a good or a bad thing, it's up to you decide. But if you ask me, I most certainly believe the former is the one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12228968474915012903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1676966156" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1676966156" />
    <a title="Jiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana"><img alt="Jiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540380229p2/10502567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1676966156?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jiana" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana">Jiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781466892040" href="/book/show/29243670-wintersong">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1676966156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8165502920656486734">Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508' rel='nofollow noopener'>Maymin</a> ❤<br/><br/><b>Wintersong is a beautiful book. Beautiful, dark, mysterious, and captivating. It is a book that deals with a wide range of themes: Love, pain, selflessness, selfishness, sacrifice, family, music, strength, insecurity, and confidence.</b><br/><br/>Wintersong is apparently a retelling of the movie Labyrinth. I have never watched Labyrinth, so I had no idea what to expect. However, I was told it resembled the book Caraval, a 2017 favorite of mine. The first half definitely resembled it an</span>
  <span id="freeText8165502920656486734" style="display:none">Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508" rel="nofollow noopener">Maymin</a> ❤<br /><br /><b>Wintersong is a beautiful book. Beautiful, dark, mysterious, and captivating. It is a book that deals with a wide range of themes: Love, pain, selflessness, selfishness, sacrifice, family, music, strength, insecurity, and confidence.</b><br /><br />Wintersong is apparently a retelling of the movie Labyrinth. I have never watched Labyrinth, so I had no idea what to expect. However, I was told it resembled the book Caraval, a 2017 favorite of mine. The first half definitely resembled it and I think both Caraval and Wintersong were executed wonderfully. <br /><br />I was quite worried picking up this book due to the mixed reviews. I didn't want to be disappointed, and I had high hopes I'd love it. I'm so glad I wasn't disappointed. However, I'm sad I didn't love this book as much as I'd hoped. It had its ups and downs. But I did love it. <br /><br />S. Jae-Jones is a brilliant author. Her writing is absolutely <u>magnificent</u>. I was so positively overwhelmed by it. It was captivating and so beautiful and magical. Honestly, wow. Just <b>wow</b>. Her creativity, her imagination, her wonderfully flawed characters... all of it was just great.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Your music," he said at last. "Your music was the only thing that kept me sane, that kept me human instead of a monster.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Wintersong is basically split into two halves: the first half is similar to Caraval (the Goblin King takes Liesl's sister and she has to play the Goblin King's game in order to get her sister back. The second half deals with Liesl's emotional well being and how she deals with the aftermath, which was done excellently. However, during the second half is where I think the book started going a tad downhill for me. Yes, things are revealed, yet there's a lot of questions unanswered (obviously for the sequel). Something was missing, something was lacking. Some of the events and aspects weren't properly explained. Stories were thrown into the plot here and there and I still couldn't connect some of their relevance to the actual plot.<br /><br />We also see character development in Liesl. She goes from a selfless, self-sacrificing young girl to someone putting herself first. As for the Goblin King, I really liked the mysterious aura surrounding him. He's still an enigma and there's more unanswered questions about him than answered. I'm quite excited to find out more in the sequel. Finally, I enjoyed the romance between Liesl and the Goblin King. There was chemistry and I was so invested. They're great together! Yet, I was told the ending is painful and tear-inducing. Was it? Not really. I felt... neutral. I don't know why. It was sad no doubt, but it just didn't bring tears to my eyes.<br /><br />Wintersong is a beautiful novel filled with emotion and magic. Despite how it lacked in a few areas, I still think it's marvelous and I absolutely can't wait for the sequel!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8165502920656486734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
